    - Compute the product of X and the indicator of F, take the ratio of expectation of the product of X and the indicator of F and divide it by the expected value of the indicator of F. What does this computation give?
    - Compute for any positive real r, the product of r and the indicator function that I(X >= r), i.e. r I(X >= r). What inequality do you derive by taking expectations on both sides? When does equality hold in this inequality?

Compute for any positive real r, the product of r and the indicator function that I(X >= r), i.e. r I(X >= r). What inequality do you derive by taking expectations on both sides? Apply this inequality, then use the monotone convergence theorem to check this for cofinitely many independent events with sum of probabilities < infty. What lemma is proven here? State the lemma.
    - (Exercise 1.1.3) Compute the inclusion and exclusion of arbitrary sets. Then compute this in terms of an indicator function. Lastly, apply the union bound when appropriate. What inequality do you get?

What inequality do you derive by taking expectations on both sides? When does equality hold in this inequality? Now, take exponentials of all variables. What inequality do you get?
    - (Theorem 1.8) compute P(X >= lambda sigma) + P(X <= -lambda sigma) for lambda > 0, sigma is square root of Var(X). What is this equal to? Apply Markov's inequality for exponentials onto P(X >= lamdba sigma) <= exp(-t lambda sigma/2), defining t := min(lambda / 2 sigma, 1). Decompose X_i as a product of E(exp(tX_i)), and bound this by something. Use the sum of all variances of jointly independence as a result.
    - (Lovasz Local Lemma). I copied Wikipedia. Let A be an event that is a bad event in Gamma(A) in a dependency graph. A is not adjacent to events which are mutually independent. Events that are mutually dependent are adjacent to A by contrapositive. What does this mean? Compute x: A valued in [0, 1) as a measurable function. Compute x(A) multiplied by the product of (1 - x(B)) for mutually dependent bad event B in Gamma A. Then the probability of avoiding all bad events mutually dependent in A is positive. In particular, probability of avoiding all bad events is greater than or equal to the probability of 1 - x(A_i), so x is some measurable function. Substitute x(A) = 1/d+1 and obtain the symmetric version using e as a limit. Exercise: find Moser's constructive proof.

    - (Page 10) Compute the commutative diagram associated with any epimorphism from A to B.
    - (Page 11) Compute the projective objects in the power set of Z.
    - (Page 12) Compute the commutative diagram associated with injective objects.
    - (Page 13) Compute the injective envelope E(M) for any R-module M over any ring that contains M. Start by computing the dual as a hom-set from M to ? (Hint: what is the injective cogenerator in the category of abelian groups? For every abelian group A and non-zero element a in A, there is a homomorphism A -> ? that maps a to something non-zero.). Use duality to compute a canonical image of direct sums under duality.
    - (Page 15/16/17) Using the tensor-hom adjunction, compute Hom_R(M_R, Hom_Z(R^N, T)) as a tensor product. Then substitute N = R and use an isomorphism of M otimes_R R by computing the element x otimes r using the adjunction formula. Compute the result of an evaluation map taking m to ??, then compute an embedding of M to its double dual. Hence using the fact that for F a free left R-module mapping into M^, p: F ->> M^, since Hom is left exact, then p^sharp: M^^ injects into F^ has a monomorphism, then compose these morphisms to show that M embeds in an injective module. Note that this constructs an injective hull, which is useful for injective resolutions. However, it is easier to construct projective resolutions. Given a module over a ring, find a projective module that surjects onto it by taking gnerators, and computing a map from a free module and resolving the relations.
    - (Page 18) Compute a formula for the factorisation of x in terms of y for any integer n in a divisible additive group. Knowing that every quotient of a divisible group is divisible, and that every module M embeds in its injective envelope, infer that an abelian group is divisible iff it is an injective Z-module.

    - (Page 19) Compute what is E(M) if there is an essential embedding into E(M) and E(M) is injective.
    - (Page 20) Compute the image of the epimmorphism for each object in the chain associated with a projective resolution which terminates at M -> 0, check that every morphism is an epimorphism on the kernel onto its next morphism.
    - (Page 21) Compute the composition of two maps in a chain complex.

    - (Page 21) Compute the rule of maps associated with chain maps as morphisms of chain complexes.
    - (Page 22) Compute the commutative diagram associated with two homotopic chain maps. (Hint: g_n - f_n: C_n -> D_n).
    - (Page 23) Compute the factorisation of every morphism of A to B for I the image of f in the morphism f from A to B in an abelian category. Check that A is the kernel of the epimorphism and C is the cokernel of the monomorphism in a short exact sequence A and B.

    - (Page 25) Compute the homology of two homotopy equivalent chain complexes C_* and D_*, i.e. compute H_*(D*) in terms of H_*(C_*) using the definition of a functor. Prove this fact on the level of maps. using the definition of a functor.

    - (Slide 26) Compute the domain and the codomain of a finite etale map. Compute the inverse of the discriminant.
    - (Slide 28) Check that the map Spec(C[x][y]/(y^n - x)) -> Spec(C[x]) is not etale by computing the discriminant.
    - (Slide 29) Amend this map Spec(C[x][y]/(y^n - x)) -> Spec(C[x]) to make it etale.

    - (Slide 36) Compute for a map of arithmetic schemes, obtain a conjugacy class of homomorphisms.
    - (Slide 37) Compute for a map of arithmetic schemes Spec(k(x)) -> X, obtain a conjugacy class of homomorphisms.
    - (Slide 38) Compute the profinite completion of topological pi_1 for X a complex algebraic variety.
    - (Slide 40) Compute an isomorphism for X a variety in the algebraic completion over Q.
    - (Slide 41) Compute an "isomorphism" for X a variety in the algebraic completion over bar F_p. Where does this isomorphism fail.
    - (Slide 42) Compute for X = Spec(F), F a field, the fundamental group of X.
    - (Slide 43) Compute, for X = Spec(O_F), the abelianised fundamental group of X. Where O_F is an algebraic number field.
    - (Slide 44) Compute, for X = Spec(O_F), the fundamental group of X. Where O_F is an algebraic number field. Note that this is not abelianised. (Hint: compute as a limit running over...)
    - (Slide 45) Compute pi_1(X) of X = Spec(Z), what does this mean?
    - (Slide 46) Compute for X = Spec(O_F), F= Q(sqrt(-2 * 3 * 5 * 7 * 11 * 13)).
    - (Slide 47) Compute for X = Spec(O_F), F = Q(sqrt(653)), assume the generalised Riemann hypothesis, what is this?
    - (Slide 48) Compute for X = Spec(O_F), F = Q(sqrt(1429)), assume the generalised Riemann hypothesis, what is this?
    - (Slide 49) Compute for X_S = Spec(O_F)\S, S a finite set of prime ideals (recall what are prime ideals in this case), consider K/F finite Galois extensions, compute pi_1(X_S). (Hint: need contravariant Spec maps).
    - (Slide 50) Compute for X a scheme of finite type, closed points x in X_0, get a conjugacy class of elements.
    - (Slide 51) Compute for X a scheme of finite type, closed points x in X_0, get a conjugacy class of elements using the functoriality of the fundamental group. Compute that pi_1(Spec((k(x)))) in terms of a Galois group and then compute them as conjugacy class.
    - (Slide 53) Compute the completion of O_F at v, for F an algebraic number field, O_F is a ring of algebraic integers in F. (Hint, inverse limit, killing off copies of P_v^n). Compute the maximal ideal m_v for O_v in terms of classes.
    - (Slide 53) Compute the fraction fiedl Frac(O_v) in terms of pi_v.
    - (Slide 56) Compute the analogy associated with Spec(O_F) in knots and primes.
    - (Slide 57) Compute the analogy for Spec(k(v)) inserted into Spec(O_F) in knots and primes.
    - (Slide 58) Compute the analogy for Spec(O_v) in knots and primes.
    - (Slide 59) Compute the analogy for Spec(F_v) in knots and primes.
    - (Slide 60) Compute the analogy for X_S = Spec(O_F)\S in knot and primes.
